31:1330:81735:0:15:72:514:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auctions.45I then bring together the estimates from Section 4 to analyze the efficiency of bargaining.
31:1331:81837:15:16:86:525:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The  counterfactuals  hold  fixed  the  distribution  of  buyer  and  seller  types.   In  reality,  changing  the
31:1332:81951:16:15:72:525:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism could change the distribution of types participating.46Also, in counterfactuals I only change

31:1334:82153:16:16:72:525:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:trade  between  the  seller  and  high  bidder  after  a  no-reserve  ascending  auction  has  occurred.47The
31:1335:82262:16:15:72:526:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction selects the highest-value bidder, and the lower bound for the buyer’s support in the post-auction
31:1336:82367:15:16:72:525:588:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bargaining game becomesb(2), the auction price.48Finally, the counterfactual comparisons all consider
31:1337:82468:16:32:72:431:572:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:surplusafterremoving auction-level heterogeneity, both observed and unobserved.
31:1338:82547:32:22:72:285:540:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1    Solving for the Pareto Frontier
31:1339:82585:22:15:72:526:518:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:In this section I discuss how I solve for the Pareto frontier and other direct, efficient mechanisms condi-
31:1340:82692:15:16:72:525:503:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:tional on a realization ofB(2)=b(2).  By the Revelation Principle (Myerson 1979), any static, incentive-
31:1341:82796:16:15:72:526:487:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:compatible, individually rational, bilateral trade mechanism can be written as a direct-revelation mecha-
31:1342:82901:15:16:72:526:472:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:nism where players truthfully report their valuations to a broker and then trade occurs with probability
31:1343:83005:16:15:72:525:456:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f3:B:x(s,b), with the buyer payingp(s,b) to the seller.49Williams (1987) demonstrated that a bilateral bar-
31:1344:83107:15:16:72:524:441:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f7:B:gaining mechanism can alternatively be summarized by the two objects (x,q), rather than (x,p), whereq
31:1345:83208:16:15:72:525:425:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:is the expected utility for the typeS.  The ex-ante expected utility of the buyer and seller in a mechanism
31:1346:83315:15:31:72:144:410:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:(x,q) is given by
31:1347:83332:31:0:167:232:379:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f3:A:US(x,q)≡q+
31:1348:83342:0:23:234:250:392:10:g_d0_f17:7:g_d0_f15:C:∫B
31:1349:83344:23:0:240:252:369:7:g_d0_f15:5:g_d0_f19:F:b(2)

31:1352:83351:0:7:272:363:379:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f3:A:x(s,b)FS(s)fB(b)

31:1364:83446:23:15:79:525:323:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:45A “direct-revelation” or “direct” mechanism in a bilateral trade setting is one in which players truthfully report their
31:1365:83568:15:13:72:526:308:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:valuations  to  a  broker  and  then  trade  and  transfers  occur  following  allocation  and  payment  rules  which  depend  on  the
31:1366:83702:13:7:72:244:295:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:distributions of types and the players’ reports.
31:1367:83750:7:15:79:525:288:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:46For  example,  the  buyer  and  seller  types  choosing  to  attend  the  auction  house  could  change  if  the  mechanism  were
31:1368:83881:15:13:72:526:273:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:more or less favorable for certain types.  Also, the distribution of seller types could change, because embedded in the seller
31:1369:84007:13:12:72:526:260:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:valuations is the option to attempt to sell the car at the auction house at a later date, and the payoff from doing so would
31:1370:84131:12:8:72:177:248:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:change with the mechanism.
31:1371:84157:8:15:79:525:240:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:47Note that I do not work with a direct mechanism in whichNbuyers and one seller simultaneously report types to a
31:1372:84270:15:12:71:525:225:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:mechanism designer, primarily because this mechanism would be starkly different from mechanisms applied in practice and
31:1373:84389:12:12:71:525:213:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:because I wish to focus on the efficiency of bilateral trade in particular.  I also do not consider a secret reserve price in these
31:1374:84520:12:8:71:173:201:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:counterfactual mechanisms.
31:1375:84546:8:15:79:525:193:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:48Setting the lower bound of the buyer’s support to be exactly the auction price is an approximation; the actual lower
31:1376:84664:15:12:71:525:178:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:bound  of  the  support  of  buyer  types,  from  the  seller’s  point  of  view,  may  be  slightly  higher  than  this  in  post-auction
31:1377:84802:12:13:71:525:166:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:bargaining given that the buyer’s choice to not opt out of bargaining contains some information about the buyer’s type.
31:1378:84921:13:7:71:525:153:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:See the proof of Proposition 2 in Appendix A.  This approximation error will be small as long as bargaining costs are small.
31:1379:85045:7:15:79:525:146:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f8:F:49Note  that  the  notation  here  is  the  reverse  of  Myerson  and  Satterthwaite  (1983)  and  Williams  (1987),  in  whichp

31:1381:85297:13:0:72:252:118:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:for the results here.  I report it in Appendix B.2.

32:1418:86919:23:16:71:525:165:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f4:B:Note that an auction followed by the seller-optimal mechanism is equivalent to a public reserve auction.51

34:1535:91955:32:22:72:420:258:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.3    Putting It All Together:  How Efficient Is Bargaining?
34:1536:92016:22:15:72:526:236:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:This section brings together the density estimates from Section 4 and the mechanisms from Section 5.1–

35:1576:93623:15:16:72:526:358:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:by$2,000, the car will sell as long as the valuation of the highest-value buyer exceeds the auction price
35:1577:93728:16:15:72:525:342:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:by about$500.  Theg0function in the fleet/lease sample, panel (b), is slightly steeper; when the reserve
35:1578:93832:15:16:72:525:327:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:price exceeds the auction price by$2,000, the buyer and seller will agree when the buyer values the car
35:1579:93935:16:16:72:525:311:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:at  about$1,000  above  the  reserve  price.   This  reflects  the  fact  that,  in  fleet/lease  cars,  secret  reserve
35:1580:94055:16:15:72:526:295:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:prices  are  lower  relative  to  buyer  values,  and  is  consistent  with  personal  conversations  with  industry
35:1581:94171:15:16:72:526:280:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:participants, who explain that fleet/lease cars are more likely to be “priced to sell.”  Note that 7 does not
35:1582:94280:16:15:72:526:264:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:display separate results for the seller distribution upper and lower bounds because the approach described
35:1583:94386:15:16:72:525:249:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in Section 5.2 does not rely knowledge ofFS(or bounds ofFS), and instead relies directly on information
35:1584:94489:16:15:72:190:233:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:contained in reserve prices.
35:1585:94517:15:16:86:525:218:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The performance of the currently used dynamic mechanism relative to the Pareto frontier is displayed
35:1586:94617:16:15:72:526:202:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in Figure 8.  Each panel of Figure 8 also displays the location of the second-best and trade-maximizing
35:1587:94720:15:16:72:526:187:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:mechanisms with respect to the frontier, and for each mechanism pointwise 95% confidence intervals are
35:1588:94822:16:15:72:526:171:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:displayed.  In each panel, the second-best and trade-maximizing mechanisms are nearly indistinguishable
35:1589:94925:15:16:72:526:156:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:from one another on the frontier, and both lie very close to the seller-optimal point of the frontier (the
35:1590:95031:16:16:72:526:140:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:far-right point).  Figure 8 suggests that the frontier is approximately linear as it approaches the seller
35:1591:95137:16:15:72:526:124:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:optimal  mechanism  on  the  far  right  point  of  the  frontier.   However,  magnifying  the  plot  reveals  that
35:1592:95252:15:0:72:525:109:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the  frontier  is  actually  quite  concave  in  this  region  asη,  the  Pareto  weight,  moves  from  0.5  to  1.   In
36:1593:95374:0:15:72:526:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:both the dealers and fleet/lease samples, and under both the upper bound and lower bound of the seller
36:1594:95476:15:16:72:526:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:valuation distribution, the auction followed by alternating-offer bargaining results in a surplus level which
36:1595:95585:16:15:72:466:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:lies relatively close to the Pareto frontier, suggesting that the mechanism may be efficient.
36:1596:95678:15:16:86:525:635:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Any  gap  between  the  frontier  and  the  dynamic  mechanism  would  represent  a  deadweight  loss—
36:1597:95780:16:16:72:526:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:neither  bargaining  party  captures  this  lost  surplus.   I  refer  to  this  gap  as  the  deadweight  loss  due  to
36:1598:95900:16:15:72:526:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:limited commitment or mechanism choice, as this gap could theoretically be eliminated by committing
36:1599:95999:15:16:72:526:588:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to a static,  direct-revelation mechanism which lies on the Pareto frontier.  Figure 8 suggests that this
36:1600:96104:16:15:72:526:572:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:deadweight loss may not be large, but is still positive, and some points along the frontier would make
36:1601:96206:15:16:72:179:557:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f4:B:both parties better off.56
36:1602:96232:16:15:86:525:541:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:An additional source of deadweight loss is incomplete information.  Myerson and Satterthwaite (1983)
36:1603:96332:15:16:72:526:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:demonstrated that this deadweight loss is inevitable in bilateral bargaining with two-sided uncertainty.
36:1604:96436:16:15:72:526:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Intuitively,  both  parties  trade  off  the  conflicting  incentives  of  increasing  the  probability  of  trade  and
36:1605:96555:15:16:72:526:495:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:increasing the rent extracted from the other party, leading buyers to shade their offering price downward
36:1606:96660:16:15:72:526:479:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and sellers to shade their asking price upward, leading some trades to fail to be consummated even when
36:1607:96763:15:16:72:526:464:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the buyer values the good more than the seller.  This deadweight loss is depicted graphically in Figure
36:1608:96866:16:15:72:526:448:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:9 as the gap between the Pareto frontier and the first-best (infeasible) surplus line.  In both the dealers
36:1609:96973:15:16:72:526:433:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:sample and the fleet/lease sample, the gap is small.  In fact, much of the estimated Pareto frontier lies
36:1610:97078:16:16:72:526:417:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:within the pointwise 95% confidence band of the first-best line, indicating that incomplete information
36:1611:97181:16:15:72:372:401:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:per se is likely not the primary reason for inefficiency in this market.
36:1612:97253:15:16:86:525:386:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Table 4 contains more detailed information on these mechanisms, displaying the total expected gains
36:1613:97352:16:15:72:525:370:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:from trade, the gains to each player, and the probability of sale.  Gains are reported in units of$1,000.
36:1614:97457:15:16:72:526:355:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:The  table  displays  outcomes  for  the  first-best,  second-best,  buyer-optimal,  seller-optimal,  and  trade-
36:1615:97570:16:15:72:525:339:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:maximizing  mechanisms.   The  current  dynamic  mechanism  is  displayed  in  the  final  column.57Boot-
36:1616:97675:15:16:71:525:324:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:strapped  standard  errors  are  reported  in  parentheses.58The  percentages  in  square  brackets  in  the
36:1617:97783:16:15:71:525:308:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:second-best  column  represent  the  second-best  outcomes  as  a  percentage  of  the  first-best.   In  the  dy-
36:1618:97897:15:16:71:525:293:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:namic mechanism column,  percentages in square brackets represent the dynamic mechanism outcomes
36:1619:97993:16:15:71:525:277:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:as a percentage of the second-best.  Panel A uses the upper bound on the seller distribution and panel B
36:1620:98097:15:16:71:144:262:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the lower bound.
36:1621:98113:16:16:86:525:246:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:I focus first on the estimation using the upper bound of seller valuations, panel A, of Table 4.  The
36:1622:98214:16:15:71:525:230:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:final  column  shows  that  the  expected  gain  from  trade  in  the  current  mechanism  is$4,276,  with$548
36:1623:98324:15:16:71:525:215:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:going  to  the  buyer,$3,509  going  to  the  seller,  and  the  remainder  going  to  the  auction  house  through
36:1624:98439:16:15:71:525:199:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:fees.  For buyers,$548 can be interpreted as an expected retail markup above the auction price (net of
36:1625:98541:15:15:79:525:184:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:56Bazerman, Gibbons, Thompson, and Valley (1998) argued that real-world bargaining can potentially yieldmoreefficient
36:1626:98658:15:12:72:526:169:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:outcomes than the theoretical bounds of Myerson and Satterthwaite (1983) and Williams (1987) would predict possible.
36:1627:98774:12:13:72:526:157:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Bazerman,  Gibbons,  Thompson,  and  Valley  (1998)  reviewed  evidence  from  the  behavioral  and  experimental  literature
36:1628:98899:13:12:72:526:144:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:suggesting that more efficient outcomes can occur due to non-traditional utility functions (where one player’s utility nests
36:1629:99023:12:7:72:455:132:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:the other’s), limits on players’ abilities to mimic other types, and other features of bounded rationality.
36:1630:99130:7:16:79:525:125:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:57Because buyer and seller gains take into account fees paid to the auction house, the total expected gains from trade for
36:1631:99252:16:7:72:520:109:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:the dynamic mechanism in the first row is given by the sum of buyer and seller gains and fees paid to the auction house.
36:1632:99372:7:0:79:488:102:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:58These standard errors come from 200 nonparametric bootstrap replications of the full estimation procedure.

39:1784:102684:15:14:72:479:155:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:compared to current dynamic mechanism.  Gains are in$1,000 units.  Standard errors are reported in
39:1785:102782:14:14:72:501:141:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:parentheses and come from 200 bootstrap replications of the full estimation procedure.  Square brackets in
39:1786:102888:14:14:72:522:127:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:second-best column represent second-best outcomes as percentage of first-best.  In dynamic mechanism column,
39:1787:102996:14:14:72:498:113:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:square brackets represent dynamic mechanism outcomes as a percentage of second-best.  Panel A displays
39:1788:103098:14:0:72:398:99:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:estimates under seller distribution upper bound and Panel B under lower bound.
40:1789:103178:0:15:72:526:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:any other costs of remarketing the vehicle, which would be passed onto the final consumer in the retail
40:1790:103281:15:16:72:525:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:price), as a buyer’s valuation should be the amount he expects to make on the car.  For a seller,$3,509 is
40:1791:103387:16:15:72:526:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the expected gain from selling the car at the auction today as opposed to selling it through her next-best
40:1792:103493:15:16:72:526:635:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:option.  This next-best option includes the possibility of taking the car back to the seller’s own lot or
40:1793:103598:16:16:72:526:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:leaving it at the auction house to run again in several weeks.  Therefore,  the relatively high expected
40:1794:103702:16:15:72:526:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:gains from trade for the seller suggest that, in a complete-information world, sellers would be willing to
40:1795:103808:15:16:72:526:588:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:sell cars for much less.  The characteristic of the data leading to this result is the fact that even when
40:1796:103914:16:15:72:526:572:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the auction price falls far below expectation (based on auction-level characteristics) sellers still accept (or
40:1797:104025:15:16:72:458:557:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:not walk away from) the auction price with high probability, as discussed in Section 4.6.
40:1798:104114:16:15:86:525:541:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The estimated probability of trade in the dynamic mechanism is 0.705.  This measure comes from
40:1799:104208:15:16:72:525:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:integrating the dynamic allocation functionxD(ρ(S),B;B(2)) over all three of its arguments, as described
40:1800:104312:16:15:72:526:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in Section 5.2.  Comparing the estimated probability of trade to the raw probability of trade from Table
40:1801:104416:15:16:72:297:495:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:1 (0.710) serves as one indication of good model fit.
40:1802:104469:16:15:86:525:479:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Comparing each of the columns in panel A to each other yields several useful insights.  The first-best
40:1803:104571:15:16:72:525:464:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:surplus in panel A is$5,342, and the second-best surplus captures 99.7% of this surplus (as seen by the
40:1804:104674:16:15:72:526:448:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:percentage in square brackets in the second-best column), as was suggested by Figure 9.  Therefore, the
40:1805:104777:15:16:72:526:433:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:deadweight loss due to incomplete information is small.  The second-best probability of trade (0.831) is
40:1806:104881:16:16:72:443:417:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f4:B:also similarly close to the first-best (0.849), capturing 98% of the first-best volume.59
40:1807:104970:16:15:86:525:401:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The deadweight loss due to limited commitment can be evaluated by comparing the expected gains
40:1808:105064:15:16:72:526:386:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:from trade in final column of Table 4 to the second-best column.  In the used-car dealers sample, the dy-
40:1809:105169:16:15:72:526:370:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:namic mechanism achieves 80.3% of the second-best surplus (as seen in square brackets).  The probability
40:1810:105273:15:16:72:526:355:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of trade in the dynamic mechanism achieves 84.8% of the second-best level.  The gains to the buyer in
40:1811:105374:16:15:72:526:339:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the dynamic mechanism are 101.3% of the buyer gains under the second-best mechanism, while the seller
40:1812:105475:15:16:72:526:324:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:gains are only 73.4% of the second-best level.  However, the buyer-optimal mechanism would yield much
40:1813:105576:16:15:72:525:308:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:higher gains for the buyer (increasing from$548 to$3,631) and the seller-optimal mechanism would yield
40:1814:105678:15:16:72:341:293:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:improvements to the seller (increasing from$3,509 to$4,786).
40:1815:105738:16:15:86:525:277:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:For the most part,  the quantities in panel A are maximized by the appropriate mechanism,  which
40:1816:105834:15:16:71:525:262:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:serves as another check of the model.  Specifically, the expected gains from trade are maximized by the
40:1817:105937:16:16:71:525:246:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:first-best, followed by the second-best.  The buyer gains are maximized by the buyer-optimal mechanism
40:1818:106039:16:15:71:525:230:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and seller gains by the seller-optimal mechanism.  One exception to this good fit is the trade-maximizing
40:1819:106144:15:16:71:525:215:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism, which attains a level of probability of trade (0.868) which exceeds the first-best (0.849).  This
40:1820:106252:16:15:71:525:199:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:feature is due to the fact that the virtual valuations (φBandφSfrom Section 5.1) are not necessarily
40:1821:106352:15:16:71:525:184:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:increasing.  I address this in Appendix B.4 by imposing monotonicity of virtual valuations and find that
40:1822:106456:16:15:71:525:168:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:this corrects the ranking of first-best vs.  the trade-maximizing mechanism; however, this correction also
40:1823:106562:15:16:71:441:153:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:leads to a poorer fit in the probability of trade estimate for the dynamic mechanism.
40:1824:106647:16:15:86:525:137:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Panel  B  of  Table  4,  which  uses  the  lower  bound  of  seller  valuations,  demonstrates  similar  results
40:1825:106759:15:15:79:525:122:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:59Recall that the first-best would have trade occur whenever the buyer’s value is higher than the seller’s.  Therefore, the
40:1826:106882:15:0:72:491:107:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:first-best probability of trade will not be one, but will depend on the distributions of buyer and seller valuations.
41:1827:107001:0:15:72:526:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to panel A, with several interesting differences.  First,  under the lower bound of seller valuations,  the
41:1828:107108:15:16:72:526:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:probability  of  trade  in  the  dynamic  mechanism  exceeds  slightly  the  probability  of  trade  in  the  trade-
41:1829:107224:16:15:72:526:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:maximizing mechanism.  Second, the trade-maximizing mechanism no longer appears to outperform the
41:1830:107321:15:16:72:526:635:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:first-best.  Finally, while the second-best captures 99.2% of the first-best surplus, it captures only 92.8%
41:1831:107429:16:16:72:526:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  first-best  trade  volume,  highlighting  the  fact  that  trades  which  are  captured  by  the  first-best
41:1832:107546:16:15:72:526:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism but missed by the second-best (due to the incomplete information explored in Myerson and
41:1833:107644:15:16:72:526:588:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Satterthwaite 1983) tend to be relatively low-surplus trades, i.e.  cases where the buyer only values the
41:1834:107749:16:15:72:214:572:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:car slightly more than the seller.
41:1835:107783:15:16:86:525:557:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The qualitative findings from the dealers sample are similar in the fleet/lease sample (Table 5).  The
41:1836:107885:16:15:72:526:541:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:second-best mechanism achieves 99.5% or 98.8% of the first-best gains from trade, depending on whether
41:1837:107987:15:16:72:526:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the upper (panel A) or lower (panel B) bound of seller valuations is used.  The second-best probability
41:1838:108090:16:15:72:526:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of trade attains 96.4% or 90.8% of the first-best volume.  Comparing Table 5 to Table 4 suggests that
41:1839:108191:15:16:72:526:495:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the dynamic bargaining mechanism may be slightly more efficient in the fleet/lease sellers sample than
41:1840:108293:16:15:72:526:479:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in the dealers sample—consistent with conventional wisdom in the industry—capturing 90.9% (panel A)
41:1841:108392:15:16:72:526:464:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:or 86.5% (panel B) of second-best surplus in the fleet/lease sample.  The levels of gains as well as the
41:1842:108496:16:15:72:526:448:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:probability of trade are also higher in the fleet/lease sample than in the dealers sample.  Under the upper
41:1843:108603:15:16:72:526:433:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bound of seller valuations, panel A shows that the expected gains from trade in the dynamic mechanism
41:1844:108704:16:16:72:525:417:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:are$5,201, with buyers capturing$912, sellers capturing$4,060, and the remainder going toward auction
41:1845:108805:16:15:72:118:401:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:house fees.
41:1846:108816:15:16:86:525:386:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The expected gains from trade in Figures 8-9 and Tables 4–5 do not take into account any surplus
41:1847:108912:16:15:72:526:370:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:lost due to bargaining costs, and thus can be thought of as an upper bound on surplus under dynamic
41:1848:109011:15:16:72:526:355:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bargaining.  Appendix B.3 provides an approach for estimating a lower bound on surplus which takes
41:1849:109109:16:15:72:526:339:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:into account bargaining costs.  I find that the surplus lost due to costs in dynamic bargaining is small,
41:1850:109214:15:16:72:320:324:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:less than$25 for buyers and less than$50-100 for sellers.
41:1851:109271:16:15:86:525:308:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Further checks of model robustness as well as analyses of additional mechanisms are contained in the
41:1852:109371:15:16:72:526:293:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:appendices.  Appendix B.5 presents results analogous to those in Tables 4–5 under alternative sample
41:1853:109471:16:15:72:526:277:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:restrictions.  Appendix B.6 displays welfare results under alternative assumptions on the mean number
41:1854:109572:15:16:72:525:262:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of bidders,λ, and demonstrates that alternative assumptions forλdo not alter the paper’s conclusions.
41:1855:109673:16:16:72:526:246:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Appendix B.7.1 analyzes the efficiency of a seller bargaining with a random bidder rather than the high
41:1856:109776:16:15:72:526:230:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bidder. This mechanism changes not only what dynamic bargaining can achieve, but also shifts the Pareto
41:1857:109879:15:16:72:526:215:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and first-best frontiers as well. I find that bargaining with a random bidder is less efficient than bargaining
41:1858:109990:16:15:72:526:199:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:with the high bidder, but still achieves 70–88.5% of the second-best gains from trade.  Appendix B.7.2
41:1859:110092:15:16:72:526:184:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:contains results from an auction in which all players commit not to bargain, and in which the seller is only
41:1860:110200:16:15:72:526:168:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:allowed to accept or reject the auction price.  I find this mechanism is quite efficient.  Finally, Appendix
41:1861:110308:15:0:72:482:153:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:B.7.3 analyzes the mechanism which would maximize revenue for a monopolist auction house.

42:1912:111678:238:14:72:490:167:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:Notes:  Fleet/lease sample.  First-best, second-best, buyer-optimal, seller-optimal, and trade-maximizing
42:1913:111783:14:15:72:519:153:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:mechanisms compared to current dynamic mechanism.  Gains are in$1,000 units.  Standard errors are reported
42:1914:111889:15:14:72:512:138:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:in parentheses and come from 200 bootstrap replications of the full estimation procedure.  Square brackets in
42:1915:111998:14:14:72:522:124:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:second-best column represent second-best outcomes as percentage of first-best.  In dynamic mechanism column,
42:1916:112106:14:14:72:498:110:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:square brackets represent dynamic mechanism outcomes as a percentage of second-best.  Panel A displays
42:1917:112208:14:0:72:398:96:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:estimates under seller distribution upper bound and Panel B under lower bound.
43:1918:112288:0:25:72:173:681:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6    Conclusion
43:1919:112303:25:16:72:526:656:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:This paper examined the efficiency of bargaining from a real-world setting with two-sided incomplete in-
43:1920:112407:16:15:72:526:640:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:formation.  I developed a model and strategy for nonparametrically identifying and estimating the distri-
43:1921:112512:15:16:72:526:625:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:butions of valuations on both sides of the market without relying on a particular structure or equilibrium
43:1922:112618:16:15:72:526:609:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:solution  for  the  bargaining  game.   I  then  mapped  these  distributions  into  the  static,  direct-revelation
43:1923:112734:15:16:72:526:594:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism framework which traces out the efficient frontier derived in Myerson and Satterthwaite (1983)
43:1924:112837:16:15:72:526:578:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and Williams (1987).  I found that the deadweight loss due to incomplete information—the gap between
43:1925:112937:15:16:72:526:563:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the first-best trade line and the second-best frontier—is small in the wholesale used-car market.  I also
43:1926:113042:16:16:72:526:547:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:found that the deadweight loss due to mechanism choice/limited commitment is roughly 9–20% of the
43:1927:113139:16:15:72:526:531:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:second-best  surplus.   This  result  is  consistent  with  the  hypothesis  of  Wilson  (1986)  and  Ausubel  and
43:1928:113253:15:16:72:526:516:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Deneckere (1993) who suggested that it may be that “[dynamic bargaining mechanisms] survive because
43:1929:113352:16:15:72:410:500:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:they employ trading rules that are efficient for a wide class of environments.”
43:1930:113431:15:16:86:525:485:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The findings of this paper shed some light on the question of why bargaining may be used after an
43:1931:113528:16:15:72:526:469:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction, as opposed to sales mechanisms which are more standard in the theoretical literature, such as an
43:1932:113633:15:16:72:526:454:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction with no reserve price or an auction with a public reserve price.  In this industry, it is the auction
43:1933:113742:16:15:72:526:438:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:house,  rather  than  the  seller,  who  chooses  the  mechanism.   An  auction  house  is  a  platform  in  a  two-
43:1934:113858:15:16:72:526:423:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:sided market, required to attract both buyers and sellers, each with private information about his or her
43:1935:113963:16:15:72:526:407:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:valuation for the good.  A no-reserve auction could drive some high-value sellers out of the market.  And
43:1936:114068:15:16:72:526:392:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:while a public reserve auction is optimal for the seller, alternative mechanisms, including post-auction
43:1937:114172:16:16:72:526:376:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bargaining, may be preferred for the buyer or for the auction house, and may allow the market to achieve
43:1938:114276:16:15:72:526:360:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:a more efficient allocation.  Alternating-offer bargaining in particular is a natural mechanism which is
43:1939:114380:15:16:72:526:345:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:easy for players to understand and for the auction house to implement, and which does not require the
43:1940:114481:16:15:72:526:329:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:same level of commitment as static bargaining mechanisms, which, while more efficient, require players
43:1941:114583:15:16:72:526:314:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to sometimes walk away from negotiations even when it is discovered ex-post that gains from trade exist.
43:1942:114687:16:15:86:525:298:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The nature of the wholesale used-car industry as a network of competing platforms also likely affects
43:1943:114788:15:16:72:526:283:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction houses’ choice of mechanism—both the choice of whether or not to allow post-auction bargaining
43:1944:114890:16:15:72:526:267:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:as well as the choice of fee structure.  Studying the role of two-sided uncertainty and competition among
43:1945:114995:15:16:72:526:252:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction houses in determining auction houses’ choice of mechanism would be a valuable avenue for future
43:1946:115098:16:38:72:110:236:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:research.

54:2512:137175:15:16:72:525:355:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f7:B:integration, as advocated by Judd (1998), with a large number of nodes.  Specifically, letzk,k= 1,...,K

55:2598:139936:34:22:72:267:188:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:B.3    Bounding Bargaining Costs
55:2599:139968:22:16:72:526:166:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:This section describes a simple approach to account for bargaining costs incurred during the alternating-
55:2600:140073:16:15:72:525:150:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:offer bargaining game.  The parameterδ, the probability that the game does not end exogenously, can be
55:2601:140175:15:16:72:526:135:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:estimated in the data as the empirical probability that a bargaining sequence is not incomplete (where
55:2602:140277:16:15:72:526:119:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:incomplete means the sequence is recorded as having ended with a counteroffer which was not responded
55:2603:140378:15:0:72:526:104:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to).  In practice this probability can vary from period to period.  Table 6, panel A, displays these empirical
56:2604:140490:0:15:72:525:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:probabilities for periods one through six.  In estimation below I use both an upper bound onδ,δ≡1,
56:2605:140588:15:16:71:458:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and a lower bound,δ, given by the smallest of the period-levelδestimates from Table 6.
56:2606:140674:16:15:86:525:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Bounds on the parameterscBandcSare given by cases in which a player chooses to make a coun-
56:2607:140765:15:16:72:526:635:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:teroffers.   A  necessary  condition  for  a  party  to  choose  to  counter  is  that  the  payoff  from  the  player’s
56:2608:140885:16:16:72:526:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:opponent accepting with probability one must exceed the player’s payoff from accepting the current offer
56:2609:140989:16:25:72:166:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:on the table.  That is,
56:2610:141012:25:19:272:332:578:10:g_d0_f7:7:g_d0_f4:C:δpS2−cS≥pB1
56:2611:141023:19:25:246:349:559:10:g_d0_f7:7:g_d0_f4:C:δ(b−pB3)−cB≥b−pS2
56:2612:141040:25:26:72:177:534:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Noting thatδ <1 yields
56:2613:141062:26:18:269:525:508:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f3:A:pS2−pB1≥cS(21)
56:2614:141076:18:26:269:525:490:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f3:A:pS2−pB3≥cB(22)
56:2615:141090:26:15:72:525:464:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Thus, an upper bound oncSis given by the minimum gap between period 2 and period 1 offers and an
56:2616:141186:15:16:72:525:449:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:upper bound oncBis given by the minimum gap between period 2 and period 3 offers (in cases where
56:2617:141282:16:15:72:526:433:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:such offers took place).  Rather than use the minimum over all observations, I follow Chernozhukov, Lee,
56:2618:141386:15:16:72:525:418:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and Rosen (2013) to obtain a bias-corrected, one-sided 95% confidence bound forcSandcBand treat
56:2619:141481:16:15:72:485:402:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:these as upper bounds, which I denotecSandcB.60Panel B of Table 6 displays the estimates.
56:2620:141570:15:16:86:525:387:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:These estimated bargaining costs can then be used to obtain a lower bound on buyer and seller surplus
56:2621:141671:16:15:71:525:371:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in the dynamic bargaining mechanism as follows.  LetAbe the event that agreement occurs andTbe
56:2622:141765:15:16:72:525:356:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the period in which the bargaining game ends.  LetPB,handPS,hbe random variables representing the
56:2623:141862:16:15:71:525:340:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:final, net payment made by the buyer and received by the seller, respectively, after accounting for auction
56:2624:141969:15:16:71:525:325:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:house fees.  Upper bounds on the expected gains from trade for the buyer and seller are given by the
56:2625:142069:16:26:71:247:309:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:following, which ignore bargaining costs,

62:2985:153168:0:15:86:525:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The third row of each panel uses only the first car offered for sale by a given seller on a given day,
62:2986:153270:15:16:72:526:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:addressing the concern that if a seller runs multiple cars on a given day, her bargaining strategy on one car
62:2987:153379:16:15:72:526:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:may be affected by the outcomes of her previous sales that day.  The sample size is reduced substantially
62:2988:153484:15:16:72:526:635:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:under  this  restriction,  leaving  29,465  runs  in  the  dealers  sample  and  10,934  in  the  fleet/lease  sample.
62:2989:153602:16:16:72:526:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:The estimates using the upper bound of seller valuations suggest that dynamic bargaining is less efficient
62:2990:153708:16:15:72:526:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:than implied by the full sample, capturing 76.4% of the second-best surplus in the dealers sample and
62:2991:153809:15:16:72:526:588:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:only 70.0% in the fleet/lease sample.  However, using the lower bound of seller surplus, the percentages
62:2992:153913:16:15:72:244:572:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in rows one and three are more similar.
62:2993:153952:15:16:86:525:557:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The fourth row of each panel limits the sample to cars with a blue book value lying below the median.
62:2994:154053:16:15:72:526:541:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:In each panel, row four demonstrates a lower level of expected gains from trade among these lower-priced
62:2995:154157:15:16:72:526:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:cars.  The efficiency of bargaining appears similar to the full sample.  The final row limits the sample
62:2996:154261:16:15:72:526:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to new cars (those with age below the median age).  This sample results in higher expected gains from
62:2997:154362:15:16:72:526:495:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:trade but similar efficiency implications to the full sample in most cases.  One exception is in panel A of
62:2998:154469:16:15:72:526:479:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Table 8, which demonstrates that using the upper bound of the seller distribution implies that dynamic
62:2999:154571:15:16:72:321:464:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bargaining only captures 76% of the second-best surplus.
62:3000:154627:16:15:86:525:448:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The second column of Tables 8 and 9 displays the raw probability of trade within the sample.  Com-

62:3002:154827:16:16:72:526:417:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:comes  from  integrating  the  estimated  allocation  function  over  buyer  values,  seller  values,  and  auction
62:3003:154942:16:32:72:307:401:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:prices.  In both tables the columns agree quite closely.
62:3004:154998:32:22:72:437:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:B.6    Robustness to Assumption on Mean Number of Bidders
62:3005:155055:22:15:72:525:347:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Tables 10–11 display the welfare estimates using the full sample under alternative choices ofλ, the mean
62:3006:155159:15:16:72:526:332:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:number of bidders at the auction.  The main results of the paper, and all results other than Tables 10–11,
62:3007:155265:16:15:72:525:316:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:useλ= 7 for the dealers sample andλ= 10 for the fleet/lease sample.  As shown in Tables 10–11, the
62:3008:155363:15:32:72:285:301:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:welfare estimates are not sensitive to this choice.
62:3009:155414:32:22:72:248:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:B.7    Alternative Mechanisms
62:3010:155443:22:22:72:274:247:10:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f12:C:B.7.1  Bargaining with Random Bidder
62:3011:155479:22:16:72:526:225:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Table 12 displays the welfare estimates in a setting where bargaining takes place between the seller and a
62:3012:155585:16:15:72:526:209:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:random bidder rather than the high-value bidder.  Note that this setting will shift not only the outcomes
62:3013:155690:15:16:72:425:194:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:achieved in dynamic bargaining, but also the first-best and second-best frontiers.
62:3014:155772:16:15:86:525:178:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:This setting is simple to simulate for the static mechanisms simply by dropping the integration over
62:3015:155872:15:16:72:526:163:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the auction price in equations (13) and (14) and setting the lower bound of the support of the buyer type
62:3016:155977:16:16:72:525:147:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in the bargaining game to the lower bound of buyer valuations,B.  That is, bargaining with a random
62:3017:156076:16:15:72:526:131:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bidder is equivalent to an auction followed by bargaining where the auction price was the lowest possible
62:3018:156181:15:0:72:333:116:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:price and hence yielded no truncation of the buyer support.

67:3246:166111:0:15:86:525:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:For the dynamic mechanism, bargaining with a random bidder is more difficult to simulate accurately
67:3247:166210:15:16:72:526:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:without estimating a model yielding predictions of equilibrium bargaining behavior, which, as highlighted
67:3248:166315:16:15:72:526:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:above, is infeasible. However, following the argument in Section 5.2, the allocation function in the dynamic
67:3249:166423:15:16:72:525:635:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bargaining is identified for any value of Ψ =R−B(2).  Therefore,  I evaluate the expected gains from
67:3250:166523:16:16:72:444:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:trade by integrating over buyer types and seller types, setting the auction price toB.
67:3251:166609:16:15:86:525:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Table 12 presents the results.  Panel A1 displays the results for the dealers sample using the seller
67:3252:166710:15:16:72:526:588:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:distribution upper bound, and shows that second-best bargaining with a random bidder captures 96.8%
67:3253:166809:16:15:72:526:572:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of the first-best surplus.  This suggests that, even in the absence of an auction which selects the high-value
67:3254:166919:15:16:72:526:557:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:bidder, the deadweight loss due to incomplete information may not be large.  The deadweight loss due to
67:3255:167022:16:15:72:526:541:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:limited commitment does not appear to increase in panel A1 relative to the main results in Table 4, as the
67:3256:167128:15:16:72:526:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic mechanism captures 86.4% of the second-best surplus.  In panel A2, using the seller distribution
67:3257:167232:16:15:72:526:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:lower bound, the dynamic mechanism only achieves 70.5% of the second-best level.  The results for the
67:3258:167333:15:16:72:391:495:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:expected gains from trade in the fleet/lease sample (panel B) are similar.
67:3259:167407:16:15:86:525:479:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The results in Table 12 provide some evidence that the model fit is worse when the auction is ignored,
67:3260:167509:15:16:72:526:464:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:as the probability of trade in the dynamic mechanism greatly exceeds the first-best level, suggesting some
67:3261:167615:16:15:72:526:448:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:trades are occurring even the seller values the good more than the buyer.  This implies that the fit of the
67:3262:167722:15:16:72:525:433:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:allocation function,g0, is worse when conditioning on the auction price being fixed at the lower bound
67:3263:167824:16:16:72:525:417:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of the buyer support,B, than when integrating over all values of the auction price.  Also note that in the
67:3264:167930:16:15:72:526:401:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:random bidder setting, the expected transfer between the buyer and seller is not identified, whereas in the
67:3265:168037:15:16:72:526:386:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:currently used auction-followed-by-bargaining mechanism, the expected transfer is directly observable in
67:3266:168141:16:15:72:526:370:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the data.  For these reasons, I do not focus on the random-bidder-bargaining setting in the main body of
67:3267:168245:15:30:72:117:355:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the paper.
67:3268:168255:30:22:72:317:325:10:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f12:C:B.7.2  Auction Followed by Accept/Reject Only
67:3269:168300:22:15:72:526:303:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Table 13 displays the comparison of the main results from Tables 4–5 to the results from a setting where
67:3270:168404:15:16:72:526:288:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:all players can commit not to bargain ex-post and where the seller chooses only to accept or reject the
67:3271:168507:16:15:72:526:272:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction price.  As seen by the percentages in square brackets in the “Accept/reject only” column, this
67:3272:168609:15:16:72:526:257:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:alternative mechanism would capture all or nearly all of the second-best surplus and probability of trade,
67:3273:168715:16:15:72:526:241:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:suggesting that such commitment could eliminate the need for bargaining.  Conversations with industry
67:3274:168816:15:16:72:526:226:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:professionals reveal that, while this alternative mechanism is used at some auto auction houses, others
67:3275:168919:16:15:72:526:210:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:have historically found such commitment difficult to maintain, as both the high-value bidder and the seller
67:3276:169026:15:30:72:526:195:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:have incentives ex-post to negotiate when the seller rejects the second-order statistic of buyer valuations.

67:3281:169473:16:0:71:525:96:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:passes on to the seller.  These transfer functions can be defined in many ways.  One such way is given by

70:3452:176207:14:15:72:520:215:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:broker-optimal vs.  dynamic mechanisms.  Estimates from dealers sample shown on the left and from fleet/lease
70:3453:176316:15:26:72:153:200:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:sample on the right.
70:3454:176336:26:16:86:525:174:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The performance of this mechanism relative to the dynamic mechanism is shown in Table 14.  The
70:3455:176430:16:15:72:526:158:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:expected revenue for the auction house in the dynamic mechanism is estimated using data on fees when
70:3456:176530:15:16:72:526:143:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:trade occurs.  Table 14 demonstrates that, in the dealers sample, the broker-optimal mechanism would
70:3457:176630:16:16:72:525:127:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:result in auction house revenues of$3,712 under the seller distribution upper bound, and$1,824 under the
70:3458:176734:16:15:72:526:111:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:seller distribution lower bound.  Under the current dynamic mechanism, these revenues are much lower,
70:3459:176835:15:0:72:526:96:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:at$219.  The comparison is similar in the fleet/lease sample.  Both buyer gains and seller gains would be
71:3460:176942:0:15:72:526:681:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:much lower in the broker-optimal mechanism, as the majority of surplus would be taken by the auction
71:3461:177042:15:16:72:526:666:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:house.  The probability of trade would also decrease, from about 0.70 to 0.352–0.631 in the dealers sample,
71:3462:177149:16:15:72:526:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and from about 0.76 to 0.451–0.697 in the fleet/lease sample.  Comparing the total expected gains from
71:3463:177251:15:16:72:526:635:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:trade in the broker-optimal mechanism to the second-best from Tables 4–5 highlights that this mechanism
71:3464:177354:16:16:72:446:619:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:introduces an additional deadweight loss due to the broker’s rent-extraction behavior.
71:3465:177440:16:15:86:525:603:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:It is difficult to interpret these results given that a shift to this mechanism would likely drive buyers
71:3466:177545:15:16:72:526:588:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and sellers away from the auction house and toward competing sourcing venues, and this competition is
71:3467:177646:16:15:72:526:572:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:not expressed in the model.  Therefore, while auction house revenue is clearly of primary interest to the
71:3468:177751:15:16:72:526:557:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction house, competition among auction houses may impede an individual auction house from achieving
71:3469:177852:16:15:72:526:541:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the payoff of the broker-optimal mechanism.  Townsend (1983) demonstrated, in a general equilibrium
71:3470:177951:15:16:72:526:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:framework,  that  competition  among  auction  houses,  or  even  the  threat  of  competition,  leads  to  the
71:3471:178062:16:15:72:526:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Walrasian equilibrium as the number of buyers and sellers grows large.  Thus, auction houses may appear
71:3472:178165:15:16:72:526:495:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to behave as though they were maximizing surplus rather than achieving the optimal revenue for a solo
71:3473:178266:16:15:72:526:479:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:auction  house.   However,  Economides  and  Siow  (1988)  showed,  in  a  competition-on-a-line  framework,
71:3474:178374:15:16:72:526:464:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:that  liquidity  provides  positive  externalities  for  buyers  and  sellers  which  are  not  fully  internalized  by
71:3475:178493:16:15:72:526:448:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the auction house, and this may prevent efficient entry of auction houses and hence prevent the market
71:3476:178595:15:16:72:526:433:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:from achieving the surplus-maximizing allocation.  It is theoretically ambiguous how close auction houses
71:3477:178700:16:16:72:526:417:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:would come to achieving the revenue-maximizing outcomes in a setting with two-sided uncertainty.  For
71:3478:178801:16:15:72:526:401:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:these reasons, and due to the fact that I have no data on competing auction houses, I do not focus on
71:3479:178902:15:0:72:264:386:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:this mechanism in the main body of results.
